Just ate there. Having the option of white or brown rice or a salad mix is nice. They don't use "the" authentic rice you'd get in Hawaii, which is/was Hinode, but it's close. <resp>None<//resp>< Text>
Healthy food with a Korean American leaning.
Lean in to Wildflower Cafe. It's no nonsense & you get really delicious, healthy food.
Isn't it typically difficult to find any of these characteristics at an eaterie?
Not @ Wildflower cafe.
I recall the son of the owner working here. He was a lean, good-looking young man. He didn't want a cafe serving unhealthy food. He was an athlete.
The owners made a whole lot of fresh foods; some hot, some cold. Delicious dishes like: seaweed salad, buckwheat soba noodles with veggies, marinated tofu, steamed kale salad (my favorite!) and a whole lot of protein options like cold fresh turkey, baked chicken, beef meat balls, etc.
Feeling tired or stressed? Eat better! Get your food at Wildflower Cafe.
They're at the top of the "fresh" list for sure.<//Text>

<Text>I booked an appointment online for a cut and shampoo. Traffic is usually bad, but I got to my appointment early. As I give my name, I let them know that I'm early.

I was early and I didn't want to walk the mall and miss my appointment time. I'm a licensed cosmetologist myself and work for a company that has certain protocol for appointments. I completely am aware I have to wait and I'm perfectly fine waiting.

The lady checking me in looks at me weird and grabs the stylist I'm booked with from the back and both tell me that I have to wait for her next appointment to be over with for her to see me. Something I already knew. I explained I was aware of this, no rush. I just didn't want to be late for getting to my appointment.
The stylist comes and gets me from the waiting area when she is ready. I explain that it's been roughly 2-3 years since I had my hair cut at all and the last thing I did was shave my head completely due to hair loss from extreme anemia. I explain that I want to keep layers but take off dry ends and fix the natural disconnection that happens around the ear area.

Fun fact: if you cut your hair the same length all around, it's going to grow in at the same time all around and give you layers. It's  called a 90 degree cut.

She begins to dry cut my hair. As she gets to the sides, she tells me it's thinner there and asks if I had cut my own hair recently. She also points out that I have layers in my hair. I explained again that this was because I had extreme hair loss a couple of years ago and shaved my head completely because of this. After she cutting, she just curled it a little. I didn't get washed. I felt rushed out of her chair. Maybe it was for the best because the whole experience left a bad taste in my mouth.</Text>< Time>

< review>
I foolishly got stuck in a snow bank & unfortunately learned what "high centered" means (believe me, you are better off not finding this out first hand). AAA was amazingly *un*helpful, between the automated phone menu that inexplicably does not feature "Emergency Roadside Service" as an option (Claims will get you there, for future reference) and the unavailability of their contract tower.

Thankfully the CHP referred us to Black Butte and Jeff, both of whom were fantastic. Friendly, efficient and they communicated with us throughout which was very reassuring since we were stuck in a remote area & facing a night spent in the truck if no one towed us.

Can't say enough good things - worth every penny and would absolutely use them again (but hope I don't need to).< /review>

< Review>
So let's start from the beginning. I had been on the market for a car, and I'm gonna be honest. My credit score isn't the best and I needed more than just a credit card to help raise my score. Which I have also, just to clarify, but back to the point. I was looking at drivetime because I read online that you could get approved even if your credit score wasn't so great, so I decided to give it a shot. I did the online process and began to get some persistent calls from Bri, but I decided well if they are this persistent maybe I'll give it a chance. So I called Bri back at drivetime and she asked me if I was still on the market? Yes. And she asked if I was willing to go in that night to test drive? I was. So we went in, met Bri which by the way is the best sales person there. She's attentive, easy going, answers all your questions with no hesitation, isn't pushy in any way and just gives it to you like it is. I highly recommend her! She's amazing üòä

So we initially test drove one car, but the price for the down payment was just way out of our range and drivetime has this weird program that if the price ends in 7 it's a high down payment compared to when it ends in a 5. Ask them about it. So we had to compromise for another car, which I don't mind it's a great car and the process was long and tedious, but Bri and David the manager were amazing and did everything they could to help us off the lot in that car üöó So be aware if your thinking of getting a car from drivetime follow these steps:

1. Ask for Bri - trust me she's great üëçüèº
2. If you have a low credit score be prepared to have a down payment of at least 600-1600 depending on the car you want (oh! Also no matter if the car is better than the other, depending on how long it has been on the lot plays a big factor) but just be prepared!
3. If you don't already make sure to get all your pay stubs together for at least 3 months, but if you have a direct deposit then you don't have to worry about it. Bring a bill of some sort to prove proof of residence just in case.
4. BUY INSURANCE OR GET QUOTED BEFORE HAND. Saves a lot of time.
5. Be wary, if you have a low credit score your APR is going to be high. Like double digit high, but they recommend within 6 months - 1 year once your credit score is higher. That you refinance, which we will definitely be doing.
6. If they don't have the car you want, don't worry they get new cars all the time. So always check back, and if it's in the LA area they can get it transferred for you. Our car was in Montclair, and Bri herself went to go get it.

And that's all I have to say. All in all a great experience, I just have one gripe about the place and that's the women's restroom. It smells like old mildew, so that was not pleasant at all. üò∞<//Review>
